Terri




Good Morning - the food required pulls from the stock item linked to the ingredients of the recipes. When troubleshooting, you always want to make sure the broken unit weight is accurate



08:51 AM, 05th Aug







Terri




Let me check on TR1689



08:52 AM, 05th Aug







Erica Pawletzki




Thank you



08:55 AM, 05th Aug







Terri




I see the serving measure is 5 ounce on the menu that was assigned, which would be 5.73 each based on the weight measures - the recipe is currently set at a 4.365 ounce which is 5 each.



09:12 AM, 05th Aug







Terri




I know you have the first week planned counts are complete, but you may want to correct the menu itself to the 5 each serving measure (or the 4.365 ounce) for the math to come out correctly on the food required



09:14 AM, 05th Aug







Terri




Once you have the menu corrected, you can assign again



09:15 AM, 05th Aug







Erica Pawletzki

09:16 AM, 05th Aug







Erica Pawletzki

09:17 AM, 05th Aug







Terri

Terri






09:18 AM, 05th Aug







Terri




I am seeing the same stock item



09:18 AM, 05th Aug







Erica Pawletzki




Yes, but look in the recipe and the ingredient and the stock item it's linked to and you'll see a different number.



09:19 AM, 05th Aug







Erica Pawletzki




We don't know how that's possible



09:19 AM, 05th Aug







Terri




Ok, I used the "Update Food Required" button on both the stock item and the recipe and now it is showing the correct stock item - I did also re-save the production plans



09:25 AM, 05th Aug







Terri




When they complete their plans in the future, the correct stock item should pull through for you as well

Good afternoon,

If a single ingredient recipe is linked to a stock item and an ingredient, why would it not show up under food required on the production plans?

Thank you,

Meshala Huff

Assistant Director of Child Nutrition

Email:
meshala.huff@paisd.org

Phone: 409-984-6231

Cell: 409-960-2745

CONFIDENTIALITY NOTICE:  This message from the Port Arthur Independent School District may contain confidential or privileged information. If you received this transmission in error,
 please return it to the sender and delete the material from any computer. Disclosure or use of any part of this message by persons other than the intended recipient is prohibited.

--- turn 1 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2025-09-04T18:39:24Z ---
Hello Meshala,

This could be due to the single ingredient recipe tied to a stock item that does not have a broken unit weight under the buying guide tab of the ingredient that would be preventing the system from properly calculating the amount needed. If it does have a broken unit, then make sure the recipe also has show in summary checked so the item can be shown in the production plan food required. If both are done, then let me know and also provide the recipe code if it is a specific single ingredient recipe that is giving issues. (the pictures shown below are just examples for clarity). Thank you.

1. Recalculate the Weights

Often, if you've made changes to the ingredients, the system needs to be prompted to update the total weight.

Navigate to the Ingredients tab of the recipe.

Click the (Re)calculate Weights button. This will recalculate the nutrient analysis and should update the total weight on the General tab.

You can also use (Re)calculate all Purchase Items if you've changed ingredients or steps.

2. Verify Ingredient Information

The "Recipe Total Weight" on the General tab is automatically calculated based on the ingredients you've entered. An error here is often traced back to an incorrect entry on the Ingredients tab.

Go to the Ingredients tab.

Carefully review each ingredient listed.

Check that the Quantity and the Unit of Measure (e.g., patty, slice, cup) are correct for each ingredient. A simple typo here is a common culprit.

3. Check for Moisture, Fat, and Waste Factors

Certain cooking processes can change the weight of the final product. PrimeroEdge has fields to account for this.

On the General tab of the recipe, look for the fields for Moisture and Fat Change (%) and Waste Factor.

These fields are optional but crucial for accuracy with certain foods.

Moisture/Fat: For example, pasta gains moisture and weight when cooked, while ground beef loses fat and weight.

Waste: An item like a watermelon will have waste from the rind that should be accounted for.

Ensure these fields are filled in correctly if they apply to your recipe.

1. Recalculate the Weights

Often, if you've made changes to the ingredients, the system needs to be prompted to update the total weight.

Navigate to the Ingredients tab of the recipe.

Click the (Re)calculate Weights button. This will recalculate the nutrient analysis and should update the total weight on the General tab.

You can also use (Re)calculate all Purchase Items if you've changed ingredients or steps.

2. Verify Ingredient Information

The "Recipe Total Weight" on the General tab is automatically calculated based on the ingredients you've entered. An error here is often traced back to an incorrect entry on the Ingredients tab.

Go to the Ingredients tab.

Carefully review each ingredient listed.

Check that the Quantity and the Unit of Measure (e.g., patty, slice, cup) are correct for each ingredient. A simple typo here is a common culprit.

3. Check for Moisture, Fat, and Waste Factors

Certain cooking processes can change the weight of the final product. PrimeroEdge has fields to account for this.

On the General tab of the recipe, look for the fields for Moisture and Fat Change (%) and Waste Factor.

These fields are optional but crucial for accuracy with certain foods.

Moisture/Fat: For example, pasta gains moisture and weight when cooked, while ground beef loses fat and weight.

Waste: An item like a watermelon will have waste from the rind that should be accounted for.

Ensure these fields are filled in correctly if they apply to your recipe.

--- turn 2 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2025-10-23T11:53:47Z ---
Hello Tanya,

You should be able to click the pencil next to the 1/4 cup to edit the grams there, and it will flow through to the nutrients for your 2 teaspoons.

There are 12 teaspoons in a 1/4 cup.

Based on your statement that 2 teaspoons should be 5 grams, that means that each teaspoon is 2.5 grams.

12 teaspoons at 2.5 grams = 30 grams

So changing the 1/4 cup to 30 grams should update the nutrients tab to the 5 grams that you're expecting.

TICKET 304911  |  5 - Orangefield ISD - Ingredients
==========================================================================================

--- turn 0 [customer/description] Sandy Bland <1067609418083309@freshchat.com>  2025-11-17T18:04:45Z ---
Sandy Bland




How to delete an ingredient from a recipe?



11:53 AM, 17th Nov







Keith




Navigate to the Recipe:

Go to Menu Planning > Ingredients > Recipes.

Search for and select the recipe you wish to modify.

Access the Ingredients Tab:

Click on the Ingredients tab within the recipe record.

Delete the Ingredient:

Locate the list of Steps (ingredients) added to the recipe.

Find the specific ingredient you want to remove.

Click the Delete icon (typically represented by a trash can or delete symbol) in the row corresponding to that ingredient.

Save Changes:

Confirm the deletion if prompted.

Ensure you Save the recipe to apply the changes permanently.



11:56 AM, 17th Nov

Team Inbox

Cant figure out why LI100321 Ground Paprika shows weird quantities when everything is set up to be 1  tablespoon


6.8000 grams ?

--- turn 2 [agent/private_note] agent:22052027946  2025-11-20T20:09:06Z ---
I will check with Marcus before responding to determine if it's the correct solution. Additionally, I will ask him whether I should update the setting and inform them in such cases or request that the district update it themselves.

Testing in Online 5 UAT:

When the "Method to convert Ingredient Measurements" setting for recipes is set to "Use Standard Measurements," the recipe displays paprika measurements in cups and tablespoons.

Updated the setting "Use Preferred Measurement," and the recipe report is now working as expected.

--- turn 3 [agent/private_note] agent:22052027946  2025-11-20T21:13:42Z ---
Spoke to Marcus and he approved

--- turn 4 [agent/private_note] agent:22052027946  2025-11-20T21:30:47Z ---
This issue can be resolved by updating a setting. Please follow these steps to resolve the issue:

Navigate to the system settings.

Click on "System Settings."

Select "Menu Planning."

Search for the setting "
Method to convert Ingredient Measurements
" and update it from "Use Standard Measurements" to "
Use Preferred Measurement
," then click "Save."

Return to the recipe report and refresh it. The report should now display paprika quantity in tablespoons.

Please follow the steps outlined above, update the settings accordingly, and verify the changes. If you need any further assistance, please let us know.

--- turn 5 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2025-11-20T22:31:38Z ---

TICKET 309341  |  Rio Vista ISD - broken units
==========================================================================================

--- turn 0 [customer/description] Karina Farias <kfarias@rvisd.net>  2026-01-14T17:17:18Z ---
Karina Farias




Keith I have a question. When it comes to products. I have to Add New Item first, and then from there, is when you turn it into an ingredient correct? Is that correct step process?



10:59 AM, 14th Jan







Karina Farias




and how can I edit this highlighted part?



11:04 AM, 14th Jan







Keith




You go in order, Ingredient, Recipe;



11:04 AM, 14th Jan







Karina Farias




I already tried "edit units" but it wont let me change it



11:04 AM, 14th Jan







Keith




you cant edit those



11:04 AM, 14th Jan







Karina Farias




So do I just create a new one and put that one as inactive?



11:05 AM, 14th Jan







Keith




Only we can and we do not like to do that. We suggest making a whole new one, yes



11:05 AM, 14th Jan







Keith




We do not allow the changing of broken units because it causes discrepancies in the system. If the stock item is used in inventory, changing the broken units per whole unit will severely affect the perpetual inventory, past transactions and reports in an irreversible way. Although the effect in the production module is not as severe, Food used and Food prepared values in Production records could be different for records before and after the change.

For the above reasons, we strongly advise not change broken units per case.



11:06 AM, 14th Jan







Karina Farias




thank you for clarifying that



11:12 AM, 14th Jan

















Take to
Team Inbox

TICKET 309869  |  [EXT]Production Record weights
==========================================================================================

--- turn 0 [customer/description] Meshala Huff <meshala.huff@paisd.org>  2026-01-21T17:18:48Z ---
CAUTION
: This email originated from outside of the organization. Do not click links or open attachments unless you recognize the sender and know the content is safe.

Good afternoon,

I am currently in the process of fixing a database of recipes, and I need to understand why some of the weights populate on the production recipe and why some do not. Below is an example:

This is Wilson's production record for 1/12/2026. The quantity prepared shows the pounds and bags for Asian Food Solutions, but that information does not translate for the Mandarin Chicken. Can you assist in troubleshooting shy the data does not correlate?

Meshala Huff

Assistant Director of Child Nutrition

Email:
meshala.huff@paisd.org

Phone: 409-984-6231

Cell: 409-960-2745

CONFIDENTIALITY NOTICE:  This message from the Port Arthur Independent School District may contain confidential or privileged information. If you received this transmission in error,
 please return it to the sender and delete the material from any computer. Disclosure or use of any part of this message by persons other than the intended recipient is prohibited.

--- turn 1 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2026-01-21T17:44:01Z ---
Hello Meshala,

I took a look at both recipes with their ingredients in mind and found the reason the General Tso's shows the weight and the mandarin chicken does not. LI101251 under the buying guide tab there is the stock item tied to the ingredient and under the broken unit weight there is a box toggle where it is left unchecked currently and this is what needs to be enabled in order for the weight to be shown on production records and hit save. The other chicken has it check marked and is the reason it shows up in production as shown below. Let me know if you have questions. Thank you.

TICKET 310433  |  Metz-[EXT]Whole Milk and Primero
==========================================================================================

--- turn 0 [customer/description] Michelle Martucci <mmartucci@metzcorp.com>  2026-01-28T20:13:01Z ---
CAUTION
: This email originated from outside of the organization. Do not click links or open attachments unless you recognize the sender and know the content is safe.

Good afternoon-

With the Gov't releasing new guidelines stating schools can now use whole milk in schools effective immediately, and that the saturated fat from the milk will no longer count toward the 10% limit on saturated fat in analysis, do you have any guidance on
 when Primero will have the capability to exclude milk from saturated fat limits?  We have districts asking about this, and am not sure how to respond.  Any info or updates is appreciated.

--

Michelle Martucci, RDN, LDN

Corporate K-12 Registered Dietitian

Metz Culinary Management

Two Woodland Drive, Dallas, PA  18612

Cell: 610-295-7903

mmartucci@metzcorp.com

--- turn 1 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2026-01-28T21:05:46Z ---
Hello Michelle,

We are aware of the new Milk Guidelines that were signed on January 14, 2026, and have been in communication with the USDA regarding the implementation. They have confirmed that the changes only impact lunch menus at this time, and we have been advised that all approved software developers will be receiving directives soon in regards to these changes.

We will be working to implement the changes as soon as we receive that directive.

Please watch the release notes for information regarding the version containing the change.  The changes will retroactively apply to the menu analysis since the ruling specified that it is for immediate adoption and use.

--- turn 2 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2026-02-20T14:16:14Z ---
Hello Branden,

In looking into the math, you have multiple things going on that aren't "math-ing" correctly.

On the ingredient - you have one case listed as over 10,000 grams.

In the inventory item, you have one case listed as containing 128 units at 3 ounces per unit.

The inventory name of the product says there are 6 bags at 4 pounds each... which does not match up with the 128 broken units of "1 each"

Does each of the 6 bags contain 128 smiley face potatoes?

So that "Broken Units" should be 6 Bags, and each broken unit (1 Bag) should be 2176 grams?

(17 grams each potato X 128 per bag based on the ingredient conversion of 4 pieces = 68 grams)

Once all of the numbers are set to correspond with each other correctly, everything will pull the way it's expected. Right now, I think the software may be confused due to the data entered.

replying all to this ticket

--- turn 1 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2026-03-02T18:11:05Z ---
Hello Lindsey,

The relationship between Whole and Broken Units is more complicated than it may appear. In the backend, we convert whole units to broken units in order to perform important calculations that involve quantity and price. Maintaining the Broken Units per Whole is important in order to preserve data accuracy and maintain inventory quantities. If Broken Units per Whole is changed for a particular item, all historical data for that item becomes inaccurate. Where you may have had 1.5 WU before, if you change Broken Units per Whole that 1.5 WU could become 2 WU. This means Inventory Valuations, Transfers, Reports, and more become unreliable and may cause all sorts of discrepancies, which will only bring about more issues that are even harder to identify.

Put simply, if an item has had any transactions with Inventory, it could be very damaging to change the Broken Units. It is for this reason that we strongly recommend creating a new item with the different Broken Units per Whole value, so the old item can be managed accurately until all remaining quantities are depleted and the item is no longer used.

With that in mind, would you like for us to go and change the broken unit?

Thank you,

--- turn 3 [agent/private_note] agent:22052027946  2026-03-09T20:59:46Z ---
Discussed with Alekya. Sending the reply per Alekya.

The current design includes sub-ingredients from all ingredients that are part of the recipes and their sub-recipes in the published menu. To include sub-ingredients only from the ingredients of the recipes and not the sub-recipes would require an enhancement request.

If you would like to submit this as an enhancement request, please inform us. We will escalate it to the product owner. We cannot provide an estimated time of arrival (ETA) for its implementation, as it needs to undergo review and development cycles. Please let us know if you have any other questions.

--- turn 4 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2026-03-09T21:00:17Z ---
Hello Molly,

The current design includes sub-ingredients from all ingredients that are part of the recipes and their sub-recipes in the published menu. To include sub-ingredients only from the ingredients of the recipes and not the sub-recipes would require an enhancement request.

If you would like to submit this as an enhancement request, please inform us. We will escalate it to the product owner. We cannot provide an estimated time of arrival (ETA) for its implementation, as it needs to undergo review and development cycles. Please let us know if you have any other questions.

--- turn 1 [agent/private_note] agent:22010986567  2026-03-17T14:55:09Z ---
Adding a note - we highly discourage them from using other district's data, but they insisted.  If they choose to use another district's data we do not get involved.  They reach out to the district and request their data.  In this instance it seems they simply changed their mind now that they realized this isn't the correct ingredients and will need to start over with entering their own ingredients.  Please remove all local ingredients.

TICKET 315348  |  OL1 - Bland ISD - Menu Planning Question
==========================================================================================

--- turn 0 [customer/description] Tracy White <tracy.white@blandisd.org>  2026-03-26T11:17:21Z ---
Tracy called to learn how to change the default ingredient measurement from 3/4 cup to 1 cup, and Chris guided her through creating a single‑ingredient recipe with a 1‑cup serving size, which resolved the issue.

Recap

Tracy explained that the default measurement for ingredients in her menu planner is 3/4 cup and she wants it to default to 1 cup for all vegetables and fruits.

Chris accessed the system, identified the broccoli ingredient codes (LI 100241 and LI 100181) and confirmed the default serving size could be changed.

Tracy created a single‑ingredient recipe for broccoli, set the serving size to 1 cup, saved it, and saw the change reflected in the nutrient view.

Tracy added the new broccoli recipe to a high‑school lunch menu, verified it appeared as 1 cup, and confirmed the drop‑down now allows selecting 1 cup.

Chris confirmed that using single‑ingredient recipes with a 1‑cup serving size is the correct approach for all fresh vegetables and fruits.

--- turn 3 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2026-03-30T17:03:19Z ---
Hello Sherry,

To fix this, search for any ingredients you’re missing. Go to
Menu Planning > Recipes
, then enter the Recipe Code or Recipe Name. Make sure the
“Include Discontinued Recipes”
 option is checked, and then activate the recipe.

Similarly, if you open a recipe and see that an ingredient is inactive, search for that ingredient in the Ingredients section and reactivate it.

--- turn 0 [customer/description] Allison Dittberner <allison.dittberner@ahschools.us>  2026-04-09T19:22:27Z ---
CAUTION
: This email originated from outside of the organization. Do not click links or open attachments unless you recognize the sender and know the content is safe.

Hello - I am wondering where we are supposed to import ingredient lists of food products in the menu planning tab.

I am able to add allergens and nutrients of a food product, however, can you share how you add ingredients in? Does it need to be in the General Tab, under "Sub Ingredients"?

Thank you,

Allison Dittberner, MS, RD, LD

Assistant Director, Child Nutrition

Anoka-Hennepin Schools

763-506-1241

--- turn 1 [agent/reply] "customercare@primeroedge.com" <customercare@primeroedge.com>  2026-04-09T19:33:26Z ---
Hello Allison,

There are two ways to import ingredients:

1) Menu Planning-->Ingredients-->Press on "Add New Ingredient" then input the information needed

2) There is an import and export function where you can download an excel template and input the data that way and then import the file to PE.

        - This could be found in Menu Planning-->Configuration-->Import/Export

Check out
PrimeroEdge

You were absolutely right in your initial email—the "Sub Ingredients" section is indeed the correct place to list that information. Adding the details there ensures they stay attached to the ingredient and sync correctly across both your menu and SchoolCafé for easy access.

Hello Allison,

To find this information, please begin by adding your custom allergen to PE. Once that is set up, you can assign it to the appropriate ingredients. After these details are saved, you’ll be able to generate an  allergen report that includes all of your custom allergens.
